Solid gold =0D=0A          =\r\n        is generally cared for in the same way </font><font size=3D\"2\"><fon=\r\nt face=3D\"verdana\"><font color=3D\"#FFFFFF\">as =0D=0A                  silve=\r\nr. Also, the =0D=0A                  =\r\nmore technical aspects of silver care have been kept to a minimum =0D=0A   =\r\n               and are more appropriate for a general audience.<br>=0D=0A  =\r\n                <br>=0D=0A                  Silver is tarnished by sulfur-c=\r\nontaining materials, particularly =0D=0A                  hydrogen sulfide =\r\n(H2S). The most common tarnish-causing elements =0D=0A                  are=\r\n wool, felt, food (eggs, onions), fossil fuels, rubber bands, =0D=0A       =\r\n           latex gloves, carpet padding, and certain paints. Tarnish is =0D=\r\n=0A                  accelerated in a humid environment. Oily salts from ou=\r\nr fingers =0D=0A                  may, if not removed, show up as corrosion=\r\n patterns that may =0D=0A                  have to be professionally remove=\r\nd.<br>=0D=0A                  If there is no tarnish present on your silver=\r\n, use a phosphate-free =0D=0A                  detergent to clean it after =\r\nuse. Silver that is used, then gently =0D=0A                  washed and dr=\r\nied immediately, will require seldom tarnish removal.<br>=0D=0A            =\r\n      Tarnish is easily removed when first noticed (usually a yellowish =0D=\r\n=0A                  tint), and will become increasingly difficult to deal =\r\nwith as =0D=0A                  it turns to light brown and eventually blac=\r\nk. Goddard&#146;s&#153; Long Shine Silver Polish =0D=0A       =\r\n           and Silver Wash, and Wright's&reg; Anti-Tarnish Silver Polish =\r\n=0D=0A                  and Silver Cream (this product offers no tarnish pr=\r\notection) =0D=0A                  are all recommended in removing heavier t=\r\narnish and residue. =0D=0A                  Use Wright's&reg; Silver Cream =\r\nto remove stains on steel knife =0D=0A                  blades. If the choi=\r\nce is between a polish that protects better =0D=0A                  but is =\r\nmore abrasive, and one that does not protect as well =0D=0A                =\r\n  but is far less abrasive, go with the less abrasive polish. =0D=0A       =\r\n           Polishes that are meant to be washed off are less abrasive becau=\r\nse =0D=0A                  they use a liquid to suspend the polishing ingre=\r\ndients.<br>=0D=0A                  Don&#146;t use polishes that have dried-=\r\nup; the abrasive particles =0D=0A                  are now much too concent=\r\nrated and will harm your silver. Never =0D=0A                  use steel wo=\r\nol (too abrasive and rust may result if not fully =0D=0A                  r=\r\ninsed from the interior of an abject), Scotch-Brite&#153; and =0D=0A       =\r\n           scouring pads (too abrasive), or dips.<br>=0D=0A                =\r\n  <br>=0D=0A                  </font></font></font>=0D=0A                  =\r\n<table width=3D\"100%\" border=3D\"0\" cellspacing=3D\"0\" cellpadding=3D\"0\">=0D=\r\n=0A                    <tr> =0D=0A                      <td align=3D\"right\"=\r\n><font size=3D\"2\" face=3D\"Verdana\" color=3D\"#FFFFFF\"><b><img src=3D\"images/=\r\nclean2.jpg\" width=3D\"280\" height=3D\"54\"></b></font></td>=0D=0A             =\r\n       </tr>=0D=0A                  </table>=0D=0A                  <font s=\r\nize=3D\"2\"><font face=3D\"verdana\"><font color=3D\"#FFFFFF\"> You =0D=0A       =\r\n           may have noticed after cleaning your silver, that a purplish =0D=\r\n=0A                  stain remained. This stain, or oxidized copper, is cal=\r\nled firestain, =0D=0A                  and can be found on many colonial th=\r\nrough nineteenth century =0D=0A                  pieces. It is not generall=\r\ny seen on pieces that have been produced =0D=0A                  by the lar=\r\nge silver companies after the 1800s, though, many =0D=0A                  o=\r\nne-man silversmithing shops still use this technique. This =0D=0A          =\r\n        depletion process leaves the object with a pure silver surface =0D=\r\n=0A                  which is more resistant to tarnishing.
